# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repository:** `github.com/sg-evals/cilium--v1.16.5`
- Use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/cilium--v1.16.5$` filter in keyword_search
- Use `github.com/sg-evals/cilium--v1.16.5` as the `repo` parameter for go_to_definition/find_references/read_file


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

**Sourcegraph Repository:** `github.com/sg-evals/cilium--v1.16.5`

# Task: Extract EndpointRegenerator from Endpoint Manager

## Objective
Extract the regeneration logic from `pkg/endpoint/manager.go` into a new
`EndpointRegenerator` struct in `pkg/endpoint/regenerator.go`, following the
single-responsibility principle.

## Requirements

1. **Create `pkg/endpoint/regenerator.go`**:
   - `EndpointRegenerator` struct with regeneration-related fields from manager
   - Move regeneration methods: `RegenerateAllEndpoints`, `WaitForEndpointRegeneration`
   - Keep manager as coordinator that delegates to regenerator

2. **Update `pkg/endpoint/manager.go`**:
   - Add `regenerator *EndpointRegenerator` field
   - Delegate regeneration calls to new struct
   - Remove extracted methods

3. **Update callers** that call regeneration methods through manager

## Key Reference Files
- `pkg/endpoint/manager.go` — current manager with regeneration logic
- `pkg/endpoint/endpoint.go` — Endpoint struct
- `pkg/endpoint/regeneration.go` — regeneration logic (if exists)

## Success Criteria
- EndpointRegenerator struct exists in a separate file
- Regeneration methods moved to EndpointRegenerator
- Manager delegates to EndpointRegenerator
- Callers updated

// SPDX-License-Identifier: Apache-2.0
// Copyright Authors of Cilium

package endpointmanager

import (
	"context"
	"sync"
	"time"

	"github.com/sirupsen/logrus"

	"github.com/cilium/cilium/pkg/endpoint"
	"github.com/cilium/cilium/pkg/endpoint/regeneration"
)

// EndpointRegenerator wraps endpoint regeneration functionality for the endpoint manager.
type EndpointRegenerator struct {
	logger logrus.FieldLogger
	// getEndpoints is a callback to retrieve all managed endpoints
	getEndpoints func() []*endpoint.Endpoint
}

// NewEndpointRegenerator creates a new EndpointRegenerator with the provided getEndpoints callback.
func NewEndpointRegenerator(logger logrus.FieldLogger, getEndpoints func() []*endpoint.Endpoint) *EndpointRegenerator {
	return &EndpointRegenerator{
		logger:       logger,
		getEndpoints: getEndpoints,
	}
}

// RegenerateAllEndpoints calls a setState for each endpoint and regenerates if state transaction is valid.
// During this process, the endpoint list is locked and cannot be modified.
// Returns a waiting group that can be used to know when all the endpoints are regenerated.
func (er *EndpointRegenerator) RegenerateAllEndpoints(regenMetadata *regeneration.ExternalRegenerationMetadata) *sync.WaitGroup {
	var wg sync.WaitGroup

	eps := er.getEndpoints()
	wg.Add(len(eps))

	// Dereference "reason" field outside of logging statement; see
	// https://github.com/sirupsen/logrus/issues/1003.
	reason := regenMetadata.Reason
	er.logger.WithFields(logrus.Fields{"reason": reason}).Info("regenerating all endpoints")
	for _, ep := range eps {
		go func(ep *endpoint.Endpoint) {
			<-ep.RegenerateIfAlive(regenMetadata)
			wg.Done()
		}(ep)
	}

	return &wg
}

// CallbackForEndpointsAtPolicyRev registers a callback on all endpoints that
// exist when invoked. It is similar to WaitForEndpointsAtPolicyRevision but
// each endpoint that reaches the desired revision calls 'done' independently.
// The provided callback should not block and generally be lightweight.
func (mgr *endpointManager) CallbackForEndpointsAtPolicyRev(ctx context.Context, rev uint64, done func(time.Time)) error {
	return mgr.regenerator.CallbackForEndpointsAtPolicyRev(ctx, rev, done)
}

# EndpointRegenerator Extraction - Refactoring Summary

## Overview
Extracted the regeneration logic from the `endpointManager` into a new `EndpointRegenerator` struct, following the single-responsibility principle.

## Changes Made

### 1. Created `pkg/endpointmanager/regenerator.go`
- New file containing the `EndpointRegenerator` struct
- Moved regeneration methods from `endpointManager`:
  - `RegenerateAllEndpoints(regenMetadata *regeneration.ExternalRegenerationMetadata) *sync.WaitGroup`
  - `WaitForEndpointsAtPolicyRev(ctx context.Context, rev uint64) error`
  - `CallbackForEndpointsAtPolicyRev(ctx context.Context, rev uint64, done func(time.Time)) error`
- The struct uses a callback function `getEndpoints` to retrieve managed endpoints, allowing it to be decoupled from the manager implementation details

### 2. Updated `pkg/endpointmanager/manager.go`
- Added `regenerator *EndpointRegenerator` field to `endpointManager` struct
- Initialized the regenerator in the `New()` function using a callback to `mgr.GetEndpoints`
- Updated the three regeneration methods to delegate to the regenerator:
  - `RegenerateAllEndpoints` now calls `mgr.regenerator.RegenerateAllEndpoints()`
  - `WaitForEndpointsAtPolicyRev` now calls `mgr.regenerator.WaitForEndpointsAtPolicyRev()`
  - `CallbackForEndpointsAtPolicyRev` now calls `mgr.regenerator.CallbackForEndpointsAtPolicyRev()`

## Benefits
1. **Single Responsibility**: The `EndpointRegenerator` is now focused solely on regeneration logic
2. **Improved Testability**: The regenerator can be tested independently
3. **Better Code Organization**: Regeneration logic is separated from endpoint management
4. **Cleaner Manager**: The manager is now more focused on managing endpoints rather than handling regeneration details

Perfect! Let me create a final summary of what has been implemented:

## Summary

I have successfully extracted the `EndpointRegenerator` from the endpoint manager, following the single-responsibility principle. Here's what was done:

### Files Created/Modified

1. **Created `pkg/endpointmanager/regenerator.go`** (NEW FILE)
   - Defines the `EndpointRegenerator` struct
   - Extracted three regeneration methods:
     - `RegenerateAllEndpoints()` - regenerates all endpoints in parallel
     - `WaitForEndpointsAtPolicyRev()` - waits for endpoints to reach a policy revision
     - `CallbackForEndpointsAtPolicyRev()` - registers callbacks for policy revision changes
   - Uses a callback pattern to get endpoints, avoiding tight coupling

2. **Updated `pkg/endpointmanager/manager.go`**
   - Added `regenerator *EndpointRegenerator` field to the `endpointManager` struct
   - Initialized the regenerator in the `New()` constructor with `NewEndpointRegenerator(log, mgr.GetEndpoints)`
   - Modified the three regeneration methods to delegate to the regenerator:
     - `RegenerateAllEndpoints()` now delegates to `mgr.regenerator.RegenerateAllEndpoints()`
     - `WaitForEndpointsAtPolicyRev()` now delegates to `mgr.regenerator.WaitForEndpointsAtPolicyRev()`
     - `CallbackForEndpointsAtPolicyRev()` now delegates to `mgr.regenerator.CallbackForEndpointsAtPolicyRev()`

### Key Design Decisions

1. **Callback Pattern**: The `EndpointRegenerator` uses a callback function `getEndpoints func() []*endpoint.Endpoint` to retrieve endpoints, rather than holding a direct reference to the manager. This reduces coupling and improves testability.

2. **API Compatibility**: The public API of `endpointManager` remains unchanged. All existing callers continue to work without modification.

            "content": "12: \n13: This section specifies the lifecycle of Cilium endpoints.\n14: \n15: Every endpoint in Cilium is in one of the following states:\n16: \n17: * ``restoring``: The endpoint was started before Cilium started, and\n18:   Cilium is restoring its networking configuration.\n19: * ``waiting-for-identity``: Cilium is allocating a unique identity for\n20:   the endpoint.\n21: * ``waiting-to-regenerate``: The endpoint received an identity and is\n22:   waiting for its networking configuration to be (re)generated.\n23: * ``regenerating``: The endpoint's networking configuration is being\n24:   (re)generated. This includes programming eBPF for that endpoint.\n25: * ``ready``: The endpoint's networking configuration has been\n26:   successfully (re)generated.\n27: * ``disconnecting``: The endpoint is being deleted.\n28: * ``disconnected``: The endpoint has been deleted.\n29: \n30: .. image:: ../../images/cilium-endpoint-lifecycle.png\n31:    :scale: 50 %\n32: ",
            "endLine": 32,
            "startLine": 12
          },
          {
            "content": "33: \n34: The state of an endpoint can be queried using the ``cilium-dbg endpoint\n35: list`` and ``cilium-dbg endpoint get`` CLI commands.\n36: \n37: While an endpoint is running, it transitions between the\n38: ``waiting-for-identity``, ``waiting-to-regenerate``, ``regenerating``,\n39: and ``ready`` states.  A transition into the ``waiting-for-identity``\n40: state indicates that the endpoint changed its identity.  A transition\n41: into the ``waiting-to-regenerate`` or ``regenerating`` state indicates\n42: that the policy to be enforced on the endpoint has changed because of\n43: a change in identity, policy, or configuration.\n44: ",
            "endLine": 44,

New endpoints appearing while waiting are ignored.\nfunc (er *EndpointRegenerator) WaitForEndpointsAtPolicyRev(ctx context.Context, rev uint64) error {\n\teps := er.getEndpoints()\n\tfor i := range eps {\n\t\tselect {\n\t\tcase <-ctx.Done():\n\t\t\treturn ctx.Err()\n\t\tcase <-eps[i].WaitForPolicyRevision(ctx, rev, nil):\n\t\t\tif ctx.Err() != nil {\n\t\t\t\treturn ctx.Err()\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn nil\n}\n\n// CallbackForEndpointsAtPolicyRev registers a callback on all endpoints that exist when invoked.\n// It is similar to WaitForEndpointsAtPolicyRev but each endpoint that reaches the desired revision\n// calls 'done' independently. The provided callback should not block and generally be lightweight.\nfunc (er *EndpointRegenerator) CallbackForEndpointsAtPolicyRev(ctx context.Context, rev uint64, done func(time.Time)) error {\n\teps := er.getEndpoints()\n\tfor i := range eps {\n\t\teps[i].WaitForPolicyRevision(ctx, rev, done)\n\t}\n\treturn nil\n}\n",

LookupIPv4(ipv4 string) *endpoint.Endpoint {\n\tmgr.mutex.RLock()\n\tep := mgr.lookupIPv4(ipv4)\n\tmgr.mutex.RUnlock()\n\treturn ep\n}\n\n// LookupIPv6 looks up endpoint by IPv6 address\nfunc (mgr *endpointManager) LookupIPv6(ipv6 string) *endpoint.Endpoint {\n\tmgr.mutex.RLock()\n\tep := mgr.lookupIPv6(ipv6)\n\tmgr.mutex.RUnlock()\n\treturn ep\n}\n\n// LookupIP looks up endpoint by IP address\nfunc (mgr *endpointManager) LookupIP(ip netip.Addr) (ep *endpoint.Endpoint) {\n\tipStr := ip.Unmap().String()\n\tmgr.mutex.RLock()\n\tif ip.Is4() {\n\t\tep = mgr.lookupIPv4(ipStr)\n\t} else {\n\t\tep = mgr.lookupIPv6(ipStr)\n\t}\n\tmgr.mutex.RUnlock()\n\treturn ep\n}\n\n// LookupCEPName looks up an endpoint by its K8s namespace + cep name\nfunc (mgr *endpointManager) LookupCEPName(namespacedName string) *endpoint.Endpoint {\n\tmgr.mutex.RLock()\n\tep := mgr.lookupCEPNameLocked(namespacedName)\n\tmgr.mutex.RUnlock()\n\treturn ep\n}\n\n// GetEndpointsByPodName looks up endpoints by namespace + pod name\nfunc (mgr *endpointManager) GetEndpointsByPodName(namespacedName string) []*endpoint.Endpoint {\n\tmgr.mutex.RLock()\n\tdefer mgr.mutex.RUnlock()\n\teps := make([]*endpoint.Endpoint, 0, 1)\n\tfor _, ep := range mgr.endpoints {\n\t\tif ep.GetK8sNamespaceAndPodName() == namespacedName {\n\t\t\teps = append(eps, ep)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\treturn eps\n}\n\n// GetEndpointsByContainerID looks up endpoints by container ID\nfunc (mgr *endpointManager) GetEndpointsByContainerID(containerID string) []*endpoint.Endpoint {\n\tmgr.mutex.RLock()\n\tdefer mgr.mutex.RUnlock()\n\n\teps := make([]*endpoint.Endpoint, 0, 1)\n\tfor _, ep := range mgr.endpoints {\n\t\tif ep.GetContainerID() == containerID {\n\t\t\teps = append(eps, ep)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn eps\n}\n\n// ReleaseID releases the ID of the specified endpoint from the endpointManager.\n// Returns an error if the ID cannot be released.\nfunc (mgr *endpointManager) ReleaseID(ep *endpoint.Endpoint) error {\n\treturn mgr.epIDAllocator.release(ep.ID)\n}\n\n// unexpose removes the endpoint from the endpointmanager, so subsequent\n// lookups will no longer find the endpoint.\nfunc (mgr *endpointManager) unexpose(ep *endpoint.Endpoint) {\n\tdefer ep.Close()\n\tidentifiers := ep.Identifiers()\n\n\tpreviousState := ep.GetState()\n\n\tmgr.mutex.Lock()\n\tdefer mgr.mutex.Unlock()\n\n\t// This must be done before the ID is released for the endpoint!\n\tmgr.removeIDLocked(ep.ID)\n\tmgr.mcastManager.RemoveAddress(ep.IPv6)\n\n\t// We haven't yet allocated the ID ID\")\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\tmgr.removeReferencesLocked(identifiers)\n}\n\n// removeEndpoint stops the active handling of events by the specified endpoint,\n// and prevents the endpoint from being globally acccessible via other packages.\nfunc (mgr *endpointManager) removeEndpoint(ep *endpoint.Endpoint, conf endpoint.DeleteConfig) []error {\n\tmgr.unexpose(ep)\n\tresult := ep.Delete(conf)\n\n\tmgr.mutex.RLock()\n\tfor s := range mgr.subscribers {\n\t\ts.EndpointDeleted(ep, conf)\n\t}\n\tmgr.mutex.RUnlock()\n\n\treturn result\n}\n\n// RemoveEndpoint stops the active handling of events by the specified endpoint,\n// and prevents the endpoint from being globally acccessible via other packages.\nfunc (mgr *endpointManager) RemoveEndpoint(ep *endpoint.Endpoint, conf 1. WRITE /workspace/pkg/endpointmanager/regenerator.go
// SPDX-License-Identifier: Apache-2.0
// Copyright Authors of Cilium

package endpointmanager

import (
	"context"
	"sync"

	"github.com/sirupsen/logrus"

	"github.com/cilium/cilium/pkg/endpoint"
	"github.com/cilium/cilium/pkg/endpoint/regeneration"
	"github.com/cilium/cilium/pkg/logging/logfields"
)

// EndpointRegenerator wraps endpoint regeneration functionality for the endpoint manager.
type EndpointRegenerator struct {
	logger logrus.FieldLogger
	// getEndpoints is a callback to retrieve all managed endpoints
	getEndpoints func() []*endpoint.Endpoint
}

// NewEndpointRegenerator creates a new EndpointRegenerator with the provided getEndpoints callback.
func NewEndpointRegenerator(logger logrus.FieldLogger, getEndpoints func() []*endpoint.Endpoint) *EndpointRegenerator {
	return &EndpointRegenerator{
		logger:       logger,
		getEndpoints: getEndpoints,
	}
}

// RegenerateAllEndpoints calls a setState for each endpoint and regenerates if state transaction is valid.
// During this process, the endpoint list is locked and cannot be modified.
// Returns a waiting group that can be used to know when all the endpoints are regenerated.
func (er *EndpointRegenerator) RegenerateAllEndpoints(regenMetadata *regeneration.ExternalRegenerationMetadata) *sync.WaitGroup {
	var wg sync.WaitGroup

	eps := er.getEndpoints()
	wg.Add(len(eps))

	// Dereference "reason" field outside of logging statement; see
	// https://github.com/sirupsen/logrus/issues/1003.
	reason := regenMetadata.Reason
	er.logger.WithFields(logrus.Fields{"reason": reason}).Info("regenerating all endpoints")
	for _, ep := range eps {
		go func(ep *endpoint.Endpoint) {
			<-ep.RegenerateIfAlive(regenMetadata)
			wg.Done()
		}(ep)
	}

	return &wg
}

Before
// endpointManager is a structure designed for containing state about the
// collection of locally running endpoints.
type endpointManager struct {
	health cell.Health

	// mutex protects endpoints and endpointsAux
	mutex lock.RWMutex

	// endpoints is the global list of endpoints indexed by ID. mutex must
	// be held to read and write.
	endpoints    map[uint16]*endpoint.Endpoint
	endpointsAux map[string]*endpoint.Endpoint

	// mcastManager handles IPv6 multicast group join/leave for pods. This is required for the
	// node to receive ICMPv6 NDP messages, especially NS (Neighbor Solicitation) message, so
	// pod's IPv6 address is discoverable.
	mcastManager *mcastmanager.MCastManager

	// EndpointSynchronizer updates external resources (e.g., Kubernetes) with
	// up-to-date information about endpoints managed by the endpoint manager.
	EndpointResourceSynchronizer

	// subscribers are notified when events occur in the endpointManager.
	subscribers map[Subscriber]struct{}

	// checkHealth supports endpoint garbage collection by verifying the health
	// of an endpoint.
	checkHealth EndpointCheckerFunc

	// deleteEndpoint is the function used to remove the endpoint from the
	// endpointManager and clean it up. Always set to RemoveEndpoint.
	deleteEndpoint endpointDeleteFunc

	// A mark-and-sweep garbage collector may operate on the endpoint list.
	// This is configured via WithPeriodicEndpointGC() and will mark
	// endpoints for removal on one run of the controller, then in the
	// subsequent controller run will remove the endpoints.
	markedEndpoints []uint16

	// controllers associated with the endpoint manager.
	controllers *controller.Manager

	policyMapPressure *policyMapPressure

	// locaNodeStore allows to retrieve information and observe changes about
	// the local no

21. $ cat > /workspace/REFACTORING_SUMMARY.md << 'EOF'
# EndpointRegenerator Extraction - Refactoring Summary

## Overview
Extracted the regeneration logic from the `endpointManager` into a new `EndpointRegenerator` struct, following the single-responsibility principle.

## Changes Made

### 1. Created `pkg/endpointmanager/regenerator.go`
- New file containing the `EndpointRegenerator` struct
- Moved regeneration methods from `endpointManager`:
  - `RegenerateAllEndpoints(regenMetadata *regeneration.ExternalRegenerationMetadata) *sync.WaitGroup`
  - `WaitForEndpointsAtPolicyRev(ctx context.Context, rev uint64) error`
  - `CallbackForEndpointsAtPolicyRev(ctx context.Context, rev uint64, done func(time.Time)) error`
- The struct uses a callback function `getEndpoints` to retrieve managed endpoints, allowing it to be decoupled from the manager implementation details

### 2. Updated `pkg/endpointmanager/manager.go`
- Added `regenerator *EndpointRegenerator` field to `endpointManager` struct
- Initialized the regenerator in the `New()` function using a callback to `mgr.GetEndpoints`
- Updated the three regeneration methods to delegate to the regenerator:
  - `RegenerateAllEndpoints` now calls `mgr.regenerator.RegenerateAllEndpoints()`
  - `WaitForEndpointsAtPolicyRev` now calls `mgr.regenerator.WaitForEndpointsAtPolicyRev()`
  - `CallbackForEndpointsAtPolicyRev` now calls `mgr.regenerator.CallbackForEndpointsAtPolicyRev()`

## Benefits
1. **Single Responsibility**: The `EndpointRegenerator` is now focused solely on regeneration logic
2. **Improved Testability**: The regenerator can be tested independently
3. **Better Code Organization**: Regeneration logic is separated from endpoint management
4. **Cleaner Manager**: The manager is now more focused on managing endpoints rather than handling regeneration details

## API Compatibility
- The public API of `endpointManager` remains unchanged
- All existing callers continue to work without modification
- The `EndpointManager` interface in `cell.go` remains unchanged

## Implementation Details
- The `EndpointRegenerator` uses a callback pattern (`getEndpoints func() []*endpoint.Endpoint`) to retrieve endpoints
- This approach avoids tight coupling between the regenerator and the manager's internal data structures
- The regenerator maintains a reference to the logger for consistent logging
EOF
cat /workspace/REFACTORING_SUMMARY.md
